Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	 We, and those of our era, apply compresses with an abundance of egg whites.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	.
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	 And indeed pierce the conjunctiva slightly, but not too deeply, but make it subtle; then apply crushed emerald as we have said; and at the completion of the work provide the patient with an agreeable bed to sleep on his back in a dark place; he should be bound from all movements, eat light foods, keep his head still, neither turning left nor right, following his condition until the third day; then discharge him into the same dim room, examine his vision, and show him various things; after that reattach the ligature up to the seventh day; it is not necessary for you to do this during or immediately after the procedure, but you should elevate it because the fluid rises quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	 If an abscess is present, on the sixth day remove the oil in front of it, and apply warmth to soothe the abscess; and once it is calmed, close the wound and place a bandage over its face for several days, keeping it in that dark room.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	 Then gradually exit the house and become one of them; know that no novices should interfere in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	Apply the oint soi qui tu est ardre de nos que tu esoie te tesmoient, nul leus a li vant se veut conter lor pais ne pas on les dous onsue que tu s’est parfait, mais quaies et prist ; et la terse en faus ei qui descez.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the resemblances of the forms of amalgamation because those who do not know them regard them as such; and they are indeed mixtures.
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en .iij. angles ague.	And let there be the essence of this same subtlety, and its counterpart in three sharp corners.
de la char sor le neis	From the cartilage at the neck
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	 At no time do various abscesses arise, of which there are some that appear like many scorpions with pus; and if such exists or has an infected wound filled with bright-colored pus, and it is swollen near the bone.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	 In that case for these joints which are loose and not dislocated, it is necessary to make the patient sit between your hands towards the sun; and work on their nostrils, and pour anointing oil into those joints, and bind them tightly; then wrap with a spatula of fine silver on one side until you know that entire joint is bone.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout .i. des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	If anything remains that cannot be closed, apply all the subtle remedies lightly, ensuring nothing is left; and if there is swelling or an abscess, treat it as required; and if malignant abscesses are present, quickly cauterize until they are cleaned out and bones exposed, then pour water, oil, or wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	 If the method does not work and moisture reaches near the palate, know that it is safe; and if moisture does not break through as needed, know there is no joint in bone above, where inflammation does not come to heal: then you must tie a linen thread slightly thickened, and keep it wet between your fingers, with space of a thumb or less; place the patient's ears under the end of the filament as best possible, and draw through odorantly until it passes within the mouth. Many times children in schools are treated this way, making it an easy task for those who know how to do so; then hold the head that comes out through the nostril with one hand, and the other head coming from the mouth with another hand, knowing each one after the other as we hold the filament.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	 Do this until you know that the worms have corrupted their blood, then draw out the blood, and moisten the thread with an Egyptian unguent, and return it to its place as before; do this for three days or more, so that the ointment dissolves whatever remains of the blood-corruption; then put a pouch of plaster on it for several days until it is healed, and if dry medicines are needed, use them; this is the way to purge the head, which allows distillation of oils and medicines into the nostrils.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait .i. mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	things as are the in, and s. 1 so
de la char sor le neis	From the cartilage at the neck
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times arises at the top of the neck a disease called "tellus," which grows and becomes visible until it can be seen; therefore, it is necessary to cut it out from the beginning, removing all the bone strongly, then placing the cautery or hot medicine on it; if it is not removed promptly as it grows large, take heed if it is hard, of sick color, lacking sensation: do not touch it with iron because it is an incurable boil, for when it is cut even once, it brings great harm to the patient; and if the boil is from a severe irritation, not of sick color, and you see that all can be covered, then relieve the patient and cut without fear, curing dry and constricting things.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	When the neck is cut and healed
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	 Know that when continuous blood flow occurs in one of these cerebral membranes, it is not beneficial and sometimes causes harm to some people.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then indeed when this happens to anyone, look to see if the wound is fresh with all its blood; and then sew up both edges of the cut, and treat until it heals; and if the edges are torn apart on either side, one must scrape off all parts of their skin so they heal, then bring together both edges of the cut, and tie, and powder over powder with dragon's blood, and burnt incense; and put over the powders a piece of aloes of strong or another kind of aloes, and let it exude through itself, then treat with ointment until healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The manner of the stitching is that you assemble the sutures: by needles as we have said in abdominal stitching; or with thread, as I have shown you.
des apostemes des levres	For abscesses on lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	When dense abscesses occur, resembling grains of pepper, small and large; then it is necessary to return the lips, cut on each side with tweezebeak, and grasp in each part; then place the liquid after vitriol incision dripping until it cools off; then provide relief and treat dryness around it until it heals.
de la char des gencives	From the decay of gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Often arises on the gums decayed, which the ancients called "albulus"; it is necessary to hold them with pincers, cut at their root, and let blood or sanguine flow; then apply vitriol incision, or other powders that restrain and dry out; if that decay returns after the incision, and often happens again, re-capping and cauterizing: it does not return after the cautery; these are the forms of ulcers to heal.
des sordens	Of sorrows
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	At no time are they gathered at the root of the teeth, within the mouth between the gums, sores that are ugly and sharp; nor do the teeth become black and yellow or blue until corruption comes to the gum, and the teeth smell bad. It is necessary for you to have the patient sit in your hands, with their heads on your altar, and pull out loose teeth or sores as they appear, until nothing remains; then make it black and green, and yellow and other colors until they are healed; and if anything that was at first reason is removed, it is good. If not, start again from the second day to the third, until you have everything extracted; and know that teeth need various kinds of medications for recovery according to what the work shows, because the rasor whose teeth fail frequently require different forms than those whose teeth are between the gums; these forms and others should be prepared with you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when you treat the tooth's pain that you delay the grinding as long as possible, because it must not always be done; for this is a very high substebisituations such that there are no excuses for extracting.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	 Then when the patient is unable to breastfeed, one must be certain of the teeth erupting.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	 Many times the pain troubles the patient, and he believes it to be a root of a tooth or gum disease, and tries pulling the rotten tooth; however, the pain does not leave until the evil forces are removed, as we have done before for such cases; and when you are well sure about the tooth aching, then it is necessary that you scrape around the tooth completely, strongly guarding the gum from all sides; then move it with your fingers or fine pliers slightly at first, until it is properly aligned, then firmly hold the pliers; and let the head of the shoulder be in thy saintly space between thine elbangs, and let it rest so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	 After extracting the tooth straight and breaking it, if it does not bleed, take any of these emollients and apply them gently inside both sides, then move it as you did first.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	 And if the tooth is pierced and swollen, it must be filled with gauze where the gums are; and delicately wedge it with pincers so as not to break while extracting; it must be carefully worked around the gum to loosen the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	 And do well to ensure that you do not break it and leave a part behind, for the patient will suffer greater pains from the root's evilness again.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	 And be aware not to do as ignorant barbers who, through haste and recklessness, often break the jawbone, without applying what we have mentioned; instead they bring great disease due to painful roots that remain or because of the bone they break, as we have often seen. When a tooth is extracted, wash the area with wine or oil and salt; and if bleeding occurs, which often happens, apply powdered vitriol there; and if this does not work, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The shapes of the strands, to which one must move the ends first, are with long points and thick knots, so they do not double when you pull the thread; and these are the forms:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And let them be large members such that they do not bend when pulled, and made of well-crafted iron wire, with teeth for easy handling.
de la racine des dens	from the roots of the strands
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	 When the root remains after fraying, it is necessary to place cotton soaked in butter at that spot for one or two days.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	 As long as the eye is softened, then apply the pincers called "algèfre", which make the head appear like a doctor's spatula; and inside they are made similarly to a file.
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with all these pliers, it is necessary that you expose the flesh entirely around the root and use the instrument called "althali", which is a lever of this form.
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And make it long and thick so that it does not break, and if the root protrudes through this, it is good; but if not, use all the instruments, from which these shapes come afterwards:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you use this instrument that has two tines, here is its shape:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	And other things related to swellings, and this instrument which appears like large pincers, whose form is as follows:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And this instrument should not be able to break; there are many swellings of swellings; and other instruments that are not counted as such. The wise master craftsmen discover by themselves their tools according to their works and the illness shows them so, for there are various diseases or no previous teacher provided an instrument for its variety, and it does not break on the wheel or other bones where they fracture; then seek swelling instruments as I have told you, and aid with gestures - this is the form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And they should be large and hold well to grasp the bone without slipping, but also to grip it firmly and remove it; then restore its original position with suitable medicines for that purpose. If there is rot in the bone, and it's small, you have all this instrument:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears not in accordance with natural law, and the shape is unattractive, especially in maidens, it must be known if the root exists behind the tooth, and is neither straight nor properly placed; then file it down. And if there's a nerve accompanying the tooth, take this instrument whose form is as shown here with a small beak, and should be made of iron pointed at both ends:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And grip the instrument lightly for days due to the hardness of the tooth and because you do not move others; if it is possible to file it down, then grind with a portion as shown in this form.
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	And it is also as the grinding of needles; and gently grind the tooth a little each day until it can be removed; then smoothly finish with a file, ensuring that if the root is too sharp and cuts the tongue, you must grind down its harshness until it is even so that it does not cut the tongue or corrupt speech.
quant li dent lochent	When the teeth are loose
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	 When the tooth is knocked out or by falling and the patient cannot press on that which they bite because it causes them to vomit, having been treated with constricting medicines but without effect; then bind them with a gold thread, for silver threads turn green and rust, but gold never moves. The filament should be of medium thickness, not too thin or too thick, according to the space between the teeth; and if you see that they are misaligned, take the wire and wind it twice around both healthy teeth, then place the head in between the teeth on either side, until you securely reach as far as the adjacent healthcuous tooth. Then resume covering up to the part where you began, and gently but firmly retract your hand, ensuring no movement; also ensure the wire is secured at the root of the affected tooth so it cannot slip out.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	 Then clamp the head of the bone with pincers, and join them, positioning between a healthy tooth, ensuring it does not touch the tongue; then leave in place as tightly as possible for as long as it can stay, and if dislocated, wind the wires around, secured by another wire; if kept in this way throughout its term, it forms two new teeth and shapes like freshly placed healthy teeth and two molars, as you see.
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And if the teeth fall out, put them back in freshly as we have said; do not interfere with someone who is neither wise nor patient, and never create a shape like an animal's tooth bone, place it where there is a gap, and restrain it as previously instructed, staying this way for long periods.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	of the tie of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	 Never is this type of wire that comes from the tongue or nature placed as such; sometimes due to accidental wounds; and the procedures are done so you work on the patient's mouth with their head in its proper position, and lift the tongue; then cut off the nervous wire along its length until the tongue is separated from its place, and if there is hardness or moisture, it is a consequence of a sore wound, where you twist up the wire at that point; and ensure the fissure does not become too wide for the artery beneath; after which, lift the lump of blood-red or cold water and apply it easily, then place a linen tent under the tongue; each night anoint the patient so that sleep cannot settle.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	 When the flow of blood persists, place vitriol poultice on it; if bleeding continues, apply slow-burning caustic to it, which is good for this purpose; then treat with other remedees until healed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it to be colored or black and hard, do not touch it as the patient does not feel it, for it is cancer; and if it starts to sink inwards with moisture, pour onion water over it, and treat it from all sides with a fine syringe, and free it from both ends; and if it persists after your treatment, apply vitriol paste until it heals completely, then return to the previous treatment until you have treated thoroughly; then raise the gauze of eased and ease water, and continue other treatments until it is healthy.
des apostemes de la gorge	Of abscesses of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	 Never does a throat swelling called "godath" occur, which are properly the two almonds; and when you treat them as we have described in our division, if not healed, be cautious: if it's an abscess of little sensitivity and soft color, do not touch with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	 And if they are red and the root is large, do not touch with iron, also for bleeding; but let it be until healed, then you will cut it out as it may break on its own; and if it's of pale color and the roots are fine, prepare the instrument to cover it up, but first ensure that the abscess is well rested and soothed.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	 Then make the patient sit facing the sun, and their head be in your hand, and work the mouth and press the foreskin between his hands, and press the tongue from all parts of the instrument; and it should be made of silver or fine iron as a knife.
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	, asse tu thet cest en pus to let not prise ande ate; then be angrys.
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	When you do not have this instrument at hand, use a pair of pliers, which is its form:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And let it be sharp on one side and blunt on the other, and when you have caught up one of the almonds, cut the other in a similar manner, then after the incision gargle the patient's throat with warm water, vinegar, saltwater, and if blood discharge occurs, gargle again with warm water or grated pomegranates or myrtle leaves; until the wound is healed. And no other abscesses appear in the throat except for the two almonds, so cut them as well.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	 And I treated a woman with an abscess inside her throat, that is to say a small abscess; and so tightly closed the entire throat that the woman could not breathe through the passage which was obstructed, and she could neither eat nor drink, and would have died if she remained thus for one or two days.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	 And the abscess was so swollen that it had risen twice by way of the two small openings.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	 I immediately approached and inserted it in the left nostril, then moved the instrument forward, taking a large portion of wax; then repositioned it elsewhere on the nose near the eyes, opened the mouth, and pressed down the tongue; afterwards I placed the catheter into these abscesses, entered one partially, and only a small amount of blood flowed out; thus was removed the obstruction in the woman's throat, and she began to drink water and then wine, continuously extracting from that abscess for long periods; as the abscesses would grow again, filling up the space I had emptied, until they became very large; then I deceived it and cauterized within her throat: thus it remained without growing. I departed from these areas, leaving only God to act upon them afterwards.
de l’uve	From the eye
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	 When they return to the eye, and it is inflamed and long, it should be called "perpendicular"; and if it is large and round, it should be called "eye".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	What is the ouem sont l’est tout lemeet, si que tu met les coure lemede ce qui emmet en la medecle. Si tu coumest li est toutes le mte coure eltie luesse li medicine tous les cheut neant de coute coton le poutrescument sont ceste li venter, si que les .i ques tellel et mete ceulements qui tout ce la medec:

Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut. de la sansue de la gorge	For throat swelling
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	 Never is there medicine without suction, as I have said in the division, by the cure of medicines; and when this does not help at all, then look into the patient's throat with sunlight, and press his tongue against the instrument that I told you about.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	 And if you see suction, grasp it with all your small hooks or fine pincers that are appropriate for this.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	 And if it is not suitable, take a reed tube and insert it into the patient's throat, then quickly remove the tube as often as needed.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	 And if the patient has consumed too much water all day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	 Then take a full cup of cold water and work on the mouth, causing it to feel as if swallowing, and move it often with his hand; and if soon after suction feels the water, let it flow out.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	 If it does not come out as we have said, gently warm the patient with aromatic substances using the instrument I mentioned in the smoke treatment of wine; do this many times, for it will gradually become less painful.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	 The manner of the smoke treatment is to place a pot where there are charcoal briquettes and cover it with a metal container, piercing through which the head of the instrument can be inserted; then you pour your fumigation into it, and the patient places the pan's handle in their mouth, sealing it so that no smoke escapes but instead goes up to the nasal cavity. The nasal cavity will now become more receptive, and if nothing comes out, begin the smoke treatment again multiple times; the patient must endure thirst, eating unsavory things and salts, and not drinking water; eventually it will be necessary for them to expel what is needed through this method.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	The form of the instrument used for throat treatment is such that it can be seen to resemble curved pincers designed for entering the throat; and like a physician's spoon, and it has roughness from lime so that whatever it grabs cannot escape. li chapistres des apostemes	The form is made of instruments resembling a physician’s tool, such as it grains, and does not:
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	 There are many kinds of abscesses, as recalled in this book from one and another, which come through puncture and cutting; there are two ways to treat them - one is the same kind but because it retains moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	 And the second way is for wounds where they lie in the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	 because an abscess on top is different from that at the base, and an abscess within a muscle is different from one in joints, each has its judgment in practice.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	 And if an abscess is not to be punctured until the swelling is completely healed; and for those that need to be pierced when they are ripe, and do not swell according to their completion, like an abscess near joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	 When an abscess comes near joints and is left to ripen around it, sometimes the tissue and nerve of the joint may be ruined, which causes contraction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	 If the abscess is near the main limb and you delay perforation until it dies, it will harm the principal limb; if it is near the foundation, pierce without waiting for it to die entirely; but one should only perforate when digestion of the abscess is complete, especially if near the foundation, ensuring it does not burst from all sides and extending within, forming a fistula.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And the pain and the9412-380.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	 In those that swell, depending on the affected limb.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	 When an abscess is ready for incision, it should be allowed to undergo full digestion before cutting, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	 For if you pierce through it, there will be spread throughout the body its poisonous blood and it is full of much filth; and by chance, the lips harden and its deep cavities.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	 And if to any abscess that are pierced according to the body's size, according to what the member requires.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	 And it is fitting to treat small abscesses with small punctures and large abscesse
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	 Those who have no head, as a superficial abscess above, it is necessary that you puncture it easily; and when the abscess is large, and has formed a great swelling, and you puncture it, do not drain all of the pus at once but only part; then bandage the abscess until the next day, then avoid any further action; perform this process gradually more each time, until the swelling is fully drained; especially if the patient is weak in strength, or a woman carrying, or small children, or elderly and decrepit men.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	 For the expectorant occasionally jumps with the discharge of pus, which may cause the patient to die; do not be concerned.

Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the method of treatment is that the patient lies on their back, and the head of the penis and scrotum are lifted up to the size of a pen'ill, so that the foreskin retracts as needed; and guard against bleeding which often occurs, and if it does occur, then use the stitching thread to close the wound until healed.
des pustules de la verge	From pustules of the penis
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a .i. oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many times these abscesses come in the penis, and it appears as an ugly blemish; there are both malignant and non-malignant ones; thus, you should puncture them with a fine needle, drain all pus, then place cotton soaked in refined Egyptian ointment on top, and cure the wound with this ointment until it heals.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	 And if the ulcer is malignant, of foul color and draining, it is necessary that you treat with a fire cautery.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	 When you have coped it, and if the ulcer is on the shaft of the penis, both inside the skin and outside, it is necessary to remove the ulcer that is within first; and when it hardens, treat the part outside.
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	 When you treat it together, do not ensure the head of the penis is pierced; darkness and decay come to the penis and its sheath; therefore, address all that is dark and corrupted before placing a poultice made from green plum bark and dates, then continue with other treatments until it heals.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	 And if bleeding occurs, prepare the moon cautery in this manner:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars; et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	 The cauterization serves two purposes together: bleeding and decay, and if the head of the penis is corrupted and retracted, then insert or conduct cotton in the penis to induce urination; and when hairs are found near the top of the penis in those who have not been circumcised due to injury or abscess, it must be scraped with a sharp instrument until all edges are freed and the head of the peneus dealt with from every aspect. If this is a serious matter, then gently cauterize near the top of the penis and hairs using a paste made with cold fresh water; then carefully separate them and apply a fine linen cloth soaked in chilled clean water without overdoing it.
de la circoncision	It pertains to circumcision.
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not a discontinuation of wounds like the others; however, when we perform this work of our own will, and properly for children, it is necessary that we make the best and easiest work for health.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not mention circumcising their children, for they do not practice it in their laws, and we have only what we have acquired through experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor .i. dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a .ij. toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	Because I have wanted the greater part of masters and saints who practiced circumcision in one day, and with force, and all newborn; it was there keys because there are two locks, and perhaps a cupboard is hung over one and another stays underne.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	When it is recaptured, the pain doubles, and in the softening which is not far from death, the point of the limb is not assured; and sometimes during the softening of the nail, the iron escapes, causing harm to the vessel, and many times this occurs so that there is no need for further treatment.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	In the softening which is done with force on all parts of the sinew, I have found the effectiveness of the experiment, as the forces cut precisely both above and below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 When you press your hand, make them equal in all the tension; but ensure the thread is well tightened around it; and keep the manner of the first operation such that you make the child think, if they perceive it, that you are only wrapping the thread around the rod just enough, and then allow him to sigh in every way possible; then let him stand upright between your hands, with his forces hidden from view underfoot or not visible at all. Then place your hand on the rod and blow or wipe, raising it as high as the head of the rod allows, cleaning it well of any dirt gathered therein, securing its knot with a double thread, then tying it below each knot; and use two strings for the pouchet and index finger, and tie them together, then release slowly without haste, as blood flows out slightly, indicating maturity. Then sprinkle powder on it and coat it thickly with glue made from a quarter of an egg well beaten with rose water mixed with oil, rich and fresh; let it stay there until the following day, treating it further until healed.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The form of cleansing is this: both sides should be held and sharpened, and the edges should be as large as a hazel rod equally.
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error of mummification is when the core inside flees to the incision; therefore, it must be stretched with your fingernail, so that the core makes an abscess; and cut evenly, and if you cannot hold it with your fingernail, then use pincers, and then cut.
Et s’il trespassent .iij. jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if they transgress for three days, and that which is below the rod is swollen, leave it until the abscess has subsided, and lightly scorch; cut as you may move, and protect the part of the rod, it will neither harm nor benefit.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore treat the sudden wound of powder, as we have said or written about powders, and if you cut beyond measure, and it goes to the top, it will not harm; treat accordingly, as we have said, until it is sound again.
dou retenement de l’urine	Holding back of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	 The holding back of urine is from a stone in the bladder, frozen blood, or bowel obstruction, or similar things we have mentioned in the division; and if the urine does not flow and you see there is retention due to a stone that is either in the bladder neck or urethra, it should be done by lying on its knees. The patient's feet are placed on their back, stretching out their stomach from above the back; they hold themselves steady as much as possible. Then one constrains the neck of the bladamo urine is released and if it does not come forth, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, then you must provide relief with a procedure using an instrument called "catheter," which consists of: fine silver wire bent like a bird's feather; the tube should be one palm wide and half again as long.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	 The method for releasing the urine is to take a double thread and tie it at the end with some wool or cotton, then insert the head of the thread into the siphon; trim off excess wool until you reach the top of the siphon, then grease the siphon with oil or butter and frankincense resin. Make the patient sit on a stool, apply oil to their bladder and penis, using moist olive oil and water at room temperature; then gently insert the siphon into the penis until it reaches near the base of the penis, then twist the penis towards the backside. Insert the siphon up to the bladamoontly, so that the patient feels relief, without following this order because the path you follow may be crooked; once all wool is removed, urine will follow the thread which can be extracted and discarded. Repeat filling the siphon until the bladder is emptied, ensuring the patient's comfort.
des maladies de la vessie	of bladder diseases
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When there are scrapes or blood enters the bladder, or rottenness is present, and you see that you must distill waters and medicines, make use of all the instrument called "clampsyr": it has this form.
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	 It is closed, and if there are three openings: two from one side and one from the other, as you see; the upper hole through which the medicinal cord is inserted so that it hangs freely without hindrance to urination, and can be pulled out when necessary, and placed where needed; and when you observe your medicine in the bladder, place the head of the catheter into the moisture, and pull up at the junction point which is there; from the catheter you will draw out the moisture to the bag, then firmly reinsert the junction point; thus the moisture will enter it now, so that the patient feels it; this is the subtle form of clistere which cleanses the bladder: such is this.
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	 It is of silver or iron, and the head is higher; from underneath at his neck the ligaments break; then take a sheep bladder and put in it the moisture that you want to administer as an enema using the bladero; then tie the two nipples with a good double thread, and heat slightly the moisture over fire; then pour into the rod the enema, then strain your hand around the bladder until the patient feels the moisture has reached the bladder; and if you do not have a bladder, take a piece of parchment, make a circle with it, and pierce roundly through; then put a strong thread into these holes, then join the circle as one would assemble a saddle, and put inside what you want of oil, moisture, and water, and tie in the instrument; and do so as you did with the bladder, pressing with your hand until the moisture reaches the bladder.
de la piere	From the stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have previously discussed in the division the methods of stone extraction and accompanying medicines; and we described the difference between stones caused by rain, and all other signs, and where one must work to cut into a stone; and regarding the bladder, and the penis; and I will now tell you clearly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont .iiij. ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that stones formed in the bladebody are more common in children and this is a sign that water leaks from the bladder like a stream of fine water; and there is often blood in urine, and men suffer with their penises, and they experience many spasms; and from such leakage, their foundations weaken; and it's easier for children to heal until they are four years old, but severe in the elderly, and moderate in those who are between youth and old age; and treatment is easier for those with large stones than for those with small ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	 When we come to treat them, it is necessary first to purify the patient with an enema, to cleanse all feces from within the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	 For it never hinders one in attempting to extract the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	 Then take the patient by the feet and lift them up straight, so that the stone descends to the front of the bladastery, and comes out without difficulty from below; then make him sit between your hands well-supported, with his hands above his thighs, ensuring that the bladastery is completely tilted downward; then grasp and probe inside. If you feel the stone in place, proceed immediately to cut around it.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	 And if it does not come out easily through probing, grease your index finger with oil from the left hand, and insert into the throat of the patient, or into their navel if they are a child, or into the middle for adults; then push firmly at its base, grasp the stone, and when you feel it on your finger, widen the bladastery's neck; then press with your finger there, and extract downward wherever you see fit.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And instruct the minister to press the bladder into his hand, and tell him to extend with his right hand the joints upward, and with his left hand remove the skin that is below the joint where the cutting occurs; then he inserts the cauterizing spatula, which gives it its form.
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	 And there is between those who are between the joints and the foundation, neither at the middle but on the left side of the neck; and it's right above the stone, and your hands should be adjacent or foundational, and support them across so that they are wide apart by necessity, and inwardly narrow, according to the quantity of the stone, not too large; perhaps press so that the hand that is between or foundational jumps without effort; and know that there may be a piece of stone or it has angles and borders: if they are grainy to remove; and if part that is loose, like wood shavings, and round, where its removal is easy.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	 If there are angles and edges, make the incision larger; and if it does not come out, then you must use tweezebarbs that resemble a file at the top, in order to extract the stone so that it doesn't escape; or place the delicate instrument curved at the top underneath it; and if you cannot manage thusly, enlarge slightly the opening a bit more until the urine flows, then strain with vitriol; and if there are more stones, first extract the largest from the bladder neck, then pull upwards, then remove deeply, and address any smaller ones afterward.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	 If it is very large, then it must be cut away, causing a larger wound.
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	 For two things happen to the patient: they die or their urine remains in place because the bladder cannot be sewn shut; however, you must exert effort with hemostasis and debridement using tweezers until it is cleansed piece by piece; once your work is completed, apply an ointment of incense and aloe and dragon's blood to the wound along with a bandage. Then cover the patient on their neck and do not remove the stitches until three days have passed.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you reset it, the joint rises quite well into place with oil and water, then heal with diaphinic unguent and basilic unguent until it is healthy again.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	 And if abscesses and ulcers come into the wound along with congealing of blood in the bladaderelief urine retention, which is known to be a kind of pain when voiding without leakage: so treat this area in the wound, and extract the sanguinenearly the bladder; otherwise it will rot and swell. Then wash the wound with water, oil, and salt until healed; you should assist him however possible until well-rested. It is essential that all bandages used to treat are fastened around his thighs, and apply medicines at the site of injury.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	 If the stone is small and it is led from the groin and inserted thusly, and urine cannot pass; if you treat as I have described here, you must dilate multiple times with this method of relieving through dilation.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	 I have already experienced such a thing.
Pren .i. foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a .iij. angles fichiees en .i. tison:	Take an iron stake according to this form and make it at three pointed ends in one piece:
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	 Then take a wire and wrap it around the groin above the stone, so that it cannot return to the bladebag; then insert the borer gently into the groin until reaching the stone; turn the borer back and forth slowly, as long as you can pierce through the other side of the stone; urine will come out soon after, then press your hand on what remains inside the groin from the stone.

The fire cautery combines two things: that is, the healing of dislocated joints and stopping blood flow, and removing moisture; then the treatment of stiff tents with fat or finely ground chalk until they are softened, allowing for repositioning of the dislocated bone; then treating wounds from sudden burns on a hard charcoal-like substance, and these remedies are dried.

des emorroydes	Of boils
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	 There are two ways of doing it: when they are within the foundation like resin grains; there can be small and large ones, and in them blood is found, either one or more; but those that recede from the foundation weaken it and at the head of the foundation; however, those who have the filaments within the foundation require treatment where you command the patient to strain to urinate until the foundation has dried up, and then threads appear; if you hurry, and cut with tweezeboar or by nail, then you sever at its roots; and if you cannot hold them due to moisture, you take a thread, silk, or a piece of camel hide; then you pull out the filaments between your fingers, cut them off, and dust hot powders that are in the place of cauterization; or you cauterize as it is said or written about cauterization, since they heal other wounds until sane; and if the foundation cannot be removed, then wash the patient with a sharp and bitter enema to cleanse what lies at the foundation, so that it can come out openly; when the patient strains, and threads are strong in the foundation, treatment is easy; and you should pull them with your nail or tweezers, cut them off, then treat as we have said until sane and avoid incision by iron.
