And when it is done, in any manner, if you must place under the seat a woolen spindle of equal length, then apply the instrument with powdered substance from the mill, including incense and egg's ash, on all around the shoulder, then strain immediately off the seat, turning the joint over the instrument, and wrap the hand at its collar, keeping hands in place like this.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés .v. jors ou .vij., et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it is necessary that he fasts so long as the limb is comforted, for then it will cure faster; and after 5 or 6 days thereafter, move it; and if it becomes firm and does not soften, then it is well-healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	 And if the joint is strongly out of place due to moisture that has occurred or another reason, you must apply three punctures with cautery as described in this chapter on cautery treatments.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés .vij. jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all this, and it remains dislocated after six days, and the joint does not hold or can lift either arm forward, then understand that the nerve at the head of the shoulder is torn or stretched or weakened; and understand that the joint will never be fixed in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The dislocation towards the back and hips is caused by impact, and extension of hands, and you provide another remedy; and treat until it is healed.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after healing comes stiffness to the limb and delays in movement, it is often used by the patient many times until those stiffnesses are alleviated and returns to its original state.
de la dislocation dou coute	Of the dislocation of the elbow joint
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	One should say that the elbow joint is dislocated at two ends and returns to both; if it's completely dislocated in all parts, especially front and back, and the dislocation is not repositioned because one can see it well and feel it; and dislocates according to each figure.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	 And when you align the affected joint with its proper position, if it appears openly visible.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	 For the joint is raised and cannot bend the arm or reach its shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	It is necessary to reset it as soon as abscesses arise, for if they come about, it would be difficult to reset them; and at times not all can be reset fully, especially when they are in the rear; these are worse than other dislocations, cause more pain, and possibly result in death.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes .ij. mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	The restoration is such that when it can be reset, extend its hand to your two hands; and spread the arms wide, and the fingers according to the cautery around, above, and below, and position the joints together or at the base of the palm until they return to their place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	When the dislocation is at the front, it returns as it folds its hand onto itself, with the root of the palm's keel that has been dislocated.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	 And if it does not return to its place, apply strong extension; and two attendants extend the arm, and wrap them with a double long and wide cloth; then turn the arm from each side; and when you have enveloped it in a cloth, pour oil on any part of the joint to soften it, then press firmly until it returns; and once it is back in place, apply dry embalmment with egg white, stretch strongly, and straighten the arm against the painful side, leaving it for several days before releasing.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	If the joint is firmly in place, release the bandage, and leave it; and if you see that the joint does not tighten well, reapply the olive oil and the bandage, leaving it for some days until it is securely fixed; then release it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	 And if after resetting the joint it feels unstable and moves, then bathe and rub well, and press until it is relieved; or place a fat sheep grease on the joint, then leave for a day and a night, then reset, and let him take a bath; and when he sweats, rub the joint thoroughly, then put the grease back on, and have him bathe again; do this twice or three times until it is well-adjusted; if you see, place moist chaff with melted butter over it and strain.
li dislocation de la main	The dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The hand joint dislocates and the return is light compared to other joints; it must be hastily returned to its place at the same hour as it dislocates, so that it swells or becomes hot like a boil.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	 The realignments are that you place the patient's hand on a table, and extend their fingers, and measure them equally, so they put their palm over the joint appearance, and hold it until it returns to its normal position; then you must ensure it is properly aligned before placing the back of their hand on an extended table for realignment.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	 And if the dislocation is in the back of the hand, place the patient's hand on a tabletop and the master fixes his hand over the appearance of the joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	 If it returns now, that's good. But if not, apply the pressure of soothing stones and let them be in such a way to begin again.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	 And if it cannot be endured, and you are unable to place it back in its proper position after any days, for the joint remains twisted; nor can anything move the fingers without moisture, or grasp any object at all: then understand that the nerves are cut, or arteries; there is no other remedy but to apply cauterization near the area and perhaps nothing else will suffice.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse .v. jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	When the hand is in place, put on the plaster as we have said, then strain and leave for 5 days, then release and keep so.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it cannot move well, and there is no cracking sound, with warm water lather, and rub until clean.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	On the displacement of fingers on the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	 Never are the two bones of the hand dislocated to either side, never from the back of the palm or the belly; then they become unstable, and cause a dislocation in your fingers as it happens, then support the head of the thumb, and push toward the part where it is dislocated; leave for three days, and then make it level again on that day; and bind it once more, as we have said, with a daily bandage, and loosen it to move, and re-bandage; do this often, until it becomes tight, and do likewise if it is dislocated in the belly of the hand, and do as you did before, until it is set right; and similarly proceed when it is dislocated from another part.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	From dysfunction of the spinal column of the back, two disorders arise: one of pain and stiffness.
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the spinal column of the back or neck is dislocated and there are several dislocations, if there is no remedy, it swiftly harms the patient.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»: li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	 And the signs are that urine flows without voluntary control, and cannot be held, and many times limbs become weakened, or knees, or one of the two arms or legs; often the spinal column slips in four parts; those where it slips towards the back are called "gilbositez": the treatment is that you must strengthen oneself if gilbositez has occurred since childhood; there is no cure nor healing for it entirely.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	 And those that come from falling or blows or similar things, according to ancient methods of treatment with many words, there is no great benefit; but I have simplified it according to my intention and created remedies in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	 In the swelling that occurs on the thighs in front, there is neither cure nor health; and similarly those that occur directly on the sides, which cannot be treated except for those properly on the back as I say; and it is so that the patient should lie face up flatly even, with strain from below without bending; then place a hot iron at the head neatly into the earth, and another at the feet, and tie a band above the affected area of the malady, and another around the calves, and knees, and ankles; and two ministers know the bands, one to the head and the other to the feet, among the two irons; and they are well fastened as we have said, with the patient's palms placed firmly on his spine, until he awakens.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	 If it does not return with this treatment, take a stick three arm lengths long, and lifted from behind the appearance, place the patient on their side, position the head of the stick under the appearance, then insert the middle of the stick along the spine; place the ends of the stick against the opposite end of the appearance, and press firmly until it returns to its place; and if you see, make the hooks at the other end turn towards the hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	 And you shall insert two sticks under the head of one arm's width on each side and between them from top to bottom, an inch wide; within each stick, there should be holes or pegs that align correctly, and they must be firmly secured so they do not move; between every two sticks, there should be a turning stick for the hooks to turn towards, with two small sticks one finger's width apart, to turn the main stick; then tie the ligaments among the joints at the end of the turning stick near the head and the other ligament toward the fingers on the opposite turning stick, and each assistant turns their respective turning stick until all are aligned, and the master adjusts the spine equally as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	 When they are equalized, place the drying agent with an abundance of heat, then the poultices, and then the splint from a tablet of three ounces in length, which points toward restoring the correct position of the swelling and the healthy part of the spine; then bind it with a bandage as we have said, and use subtle easing for the patient until they are well again; and if any issue arises at the end regarding their healing, administer medicines that soften and soothe, using the splint we mentioned earlier; never apply a piece of iron to it, nor does the appearance ever occur in the rear spine vertebrae, causing one to think it is dislocated; this is due to bone fracture, so there should be no presumption: perhaps it could bring about death.
des dislocations de la hainche	Of hip joint dislocations
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc .iiij. parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	It is said that hip and shoulder joints only come from dislocations alone, not as with other joints; the hip joint is dislocated in four parts: above and below, front and back, more internally than externally, less so in front and back.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	 And the recognition of its dislocation is such that when joining the affected leg with the healthy one, it appears longer and more bent than the sound, and the patient cannot bend their affected knee at fire; and are the legs which are swollen near an abscess hot due to the hip's head coming close.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of those who it comes upon soon, is such that this accident is contrary to those before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the sign for those who it comes upon before, is that they are well with their leg according to completion; however, not doubling the pain in his back, and if one wants him to walk, he cannot do so yet, and retains his urine, and becomes swoleby, and when it walks, he passes over the ankle.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of those who experience it later include not being able to expand their scrotum or double it, and that leg is more twisted than the other, and the pain eases, and the shoulder head is in place below the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The resetting of this type of dislocation is that you should check if the dislocation occurred earlier and it stays depending on its positioning, there is no need for treatment; and one must not have any presumption.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des .iiij. manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And in those cases where the dislocation is fresh, and there are four types of dislocations, quickly return the joint to its place, extend it forward and backward, and move it to the right and left; perhaps it will correct itself, and no further treatment is needed.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans. Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as .iiij. semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This manner of extension is common to four types, and if the dislocation returns as we have said, it is fine.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres. Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment. Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation. S’elle revient, c’est boin.	 If it returns, it is good.

When the dislocation is in front, it must be quickly extended with the affected leg, and according to what I have said; place your mirror on the pain of being above the evil limb, then press with the other hand, and extend downward toward the knee.

If the dislocation is on the other side, do not extend or lift the patient's arm, but ensure it rests as if the elbow was dislocated previously while lying down with both arms; place a splint along their face and extend using methods mentioned earlier for support over the joint; once the legs are extended and equal in length, then position pillows, straps from a bandage so that the arm does not move; rest for three or four days before unstrapping; reapply the splint underneebody; if they appear even, use the same wrapping method as before and leave for three days; afterwards, have them walk gently until fully healed.
de la dislocation dou genoil	Of shoulder joint dislocation
Li genous est desaluez selonc .iij. manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The joint is dislocated in three ways: this includes from within outwards and downwards, but not forwards.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	 Tell the patient to bend their leg towards their hip, and if it doesn't reach the hip, understand that they are dislocated; the restoration of all is that you make the patient sit up straight, extend their leg as much as possible, place your back against their face, and position their foot on top of yours. Then take hold of their heel with your hands, separate them between your thumbs, then fold both knees gently; other methods involve extending the foot until the kneecap returns to its original position, and the sign is that they can properly bend their leg towards their hip slightly; apply a plaster thereon, massage the leg against the thigh strongly for III or IV days, then release it. The patient should not move at all until the limb is reinforced.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	 And if the limb is not severely injured, then it should be gently straightened as we have said in the treatment of the elbow, until it becomes sound.
de la dislocation dou talon	For a dislocated ankle
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The heels are sometimes emaciated, and never completely realigned or properly supported.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	 And the signs are that the ankle is swollen, and one must try to move it towards the part where it was dislocated: the reductions should be gentle, and it should be extended carefully by hand when barely touched.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	 And when it is completely dislocated, you must have the patient sit upright, with the injured leg extended by your hands above the anpsle; then grasp the foot with both hands and pull gently upward twice, first to yourself, then away from you once more; elevate the foot gradually. Then place the foot firmly overhead; repeat this procedure twice as we have described, pulling and guiding the foot through its range of motion; if it returns, that is good; if not, resume the process because it will return; and if it cannot be returned in this manner, lay the patient supine on the ground with a strap securely placed between his thighs to keep him from moving while being manipulated. Next, grasp one thigh by your assistants and have them extend the injured leg towards their belt or girdle, ensuring that they support it at the knee; then gradually straighten each assistant's hand in turn, with the strap keeping the patient still as you stretch him out; next place the splints evenly to stabilize the dislocated joint while extending; finally, have one attendant perform the realignment using their hands above the injured leg.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	 And when it reaches this point, apply the bandage and pour dressings on it, stretch firmly, bind the shin to the leg, and watch for nerves behind the ankle so that the ties are not too tight; then let it be for two or three days, and if the ties loosen, strain again; then release after four days or a quarter of a day, and prevent the patient from walking for four days; and if it goes beyond this timeframe, it is not assured that it will not dislocate again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if abscesses arise, as we have said elsewhere, it is necessary to soothe them until they are healed.
des dois	Of the two joints
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When both joints are dislocated, they must be stretched carefully, it is a light task.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if the dislocation is in any of these joints, it is necessary to make the patient sit with their back and leg straight or on a table, place your foot under these joints, then press firmly on your foot until you feel relief; and when they are even, and there is no pain, place a table with two legs under the foot's sole, then strain firmpressure, and let it be for three days, then release, and allow rest until healed.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	Of wound and dislocation together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	 When a wound comes with dislocation, and you see it needs to be repaired, many times the patient dies: do not be overly confident in treatment if you are not wise in the art and have not practiced it long, nor if you are not compassebt, merciful, and slow; and begin with soothing treatments for abscesses hot, and let the sick leave to God, if you do not see hope of health; and when you see hope, now reset the limb to its place as soon as possible, that way the abscess does come out; and once the member is in place, apply calming treatments for abscesses hot, and heal the wound as it should be, with dry ointments; and if with dislocation there is a fracture, and small bones are torn loose, then perform what we have said regarding simple illnesses; and protect yourself from entering a path of fear, as I have said, for it brings consequences according to your Creator, and because of the state of your armor and body.
